Credit Portfolio Risk Monitoring & Automation Dashboard

Zahra Nur Anisah

May 19, 2026

Project Description

This project focuses on developing an interactive Credit Portfolio Risk Monitoring and Automation Dashboard using R Shiny, designed to help financial institutions monitor loan performance and detect early signs of credit risk.

The dashboard delivers comprehensive automation and analytics capabilities, such as: - Integrated Gross, Net, and External portfolios across 7 islands and 37 regions throughout Indonesia.
- Automated the tracking of key credit risk indicators, including:
- Days Past Due (DPD) buckets
- Non-Performing Loan (NPL) ratios
- Flow rate movements
- Reduced manual reporting efforts by up to 95% through automation and real-time portfolio monitoring.

Introduction

The first step involves importing all necessary libraries that support data manipulation, visualization, and the creation of an interactive dashboard.

# Load required libraries
library(dplyr)   # Data manipulation
library(ggplot2) # Data visualization
library(ggpubr)    
library(scales)  # For number formatting (commas, percentages)
library(tidyverse)  # For data cleaning and manipulation 
library(glue) 
library(plotly)  # For interactive visualizations
library(lubridate)   # For working with date and time
options(scipen = 100) # Prevent scientific notation in numeric outputs
library(readxl)      
library(purrr) # Mapping function over lists

Load Data

Before reading the three datasets (Gross, Net, and External), we first need to create a dedicated folder for each dataset on our local computer, ideally within the same directory as the project file. Each folder will serve as a dedicated storage location for the files containing the respective data.

This setup makes it easy to keep the datasets up to date, you can simply add new files to the corresponding folder, and the code will automatically detect, compile, and merge all files within that folder into a single, unified dataset.

After completing the folder setup, we can proceed to load and read the three datasets (Gross, Net, and External), from their respective directories:

  1. Gross
# Read Data: Gross
# Define the folder path for the "Gross" dataset
folder_path_gross <- "dataset/DPD NPL Gross Net Extrenal/Gross/"

# List all .xlsx files in the "Gross" folder
file_list_gross <- list.files(path = folder_path_gross,
                              pattern = "\\.xlsx$",
                              full.name = TRUE)

# Combine all Excel files into one dataframe
sqllab_gross <- file_list_gross %>% 
  map_df(read_excel)

# Read all "Gross" dataset files (including possible duplicates and NA values)

Here are the descriptions of each column in all three datasets.

  • cut_off_date: the date when the data was extracted or recorded (in YYYY-MM-DD format).
  • island: the main island or geographical region where the accounts is located.
  • region: the operational region under an island used for grouping working areas.
  • area: the operational coverage area that supervises several branches within a region.
  • branch: the branch or operational unit where the accounts is managed.
  • bucket: the category group representing loan delinquency or credit quality, usually based on Days Past Due (DPD) ranges.
  • noa: the number of accounts (Number of accounts) in the loan portfolio.
  • outstanding_amount: the total outstanding balance or remaining unpaid loan amount.

Now that we’ve read all the datasets and stored them in their respective variables, it’s time to move on to Data Cleaning & Preprocessing to ensure the data is accurate, consistent, and ready for further analysis.

Data Cleaning & Prepocessing

Here are the following steps required to clean and preprocess your dataset so that it’s ready for data analysis:

  • 1️⃣ Data Cleansing, which includes:

    • Deleting unnecessary columns or rows
    • Renaming columns for consistency
    • Changing data types
    • Adding new columns
    • Sorting data (if needed)

  • 2️⃣ Remove Missing Data (NA values)

  • 3️⃣ Remove Duplicate Data

# Data Cleansing & Preprocessing: Gross
# 1. Cleansing Data
sqllab_gross_clean <- sqllab_gross %>% 

  mutate(
    # Changing data types
    cut_off_date= ymd(cut_off_date),
    island = as.factor(island), 
    region = as.factor(region),
    area = as.factor(area), 
    branch = as.factor(branch), 
    bucket = as.factor(bucket),
    noa = as.integer(noa),
    outstanding_amount = as.numeric(outstanding_amount),
    
    # adding new column
    date = day(cut_off_date),
    month = month(cut_off_date),
    year = year(cut_off_date)
  ) %>% 
  
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date))

sqllab_gross_clean

#> #   branch <fct>, bucket <fct>, noa <int>, outstanding_amount <dbl>,
#> #   date <int>, month <dbl>, year <dbl>
# If there are any NA values, remove the rows containing NA
sqllab_gross_clean <- sqllab_gross_clean %>% 
  drop_na()

# Check the dimensions of the Gross dataset after removing NA values
dim(sqllab_gross_clean)
#> [1] 135420     11

There are no NA/ missing data in the Gross dataset

# 3. Delete Duplicate Data
# Checking if there are any duplicate data
sqllab_gross_clean %>% duplicated() %>% sum()
#> [1] 0
# If there are any duplicates, keep only the unique rows OR remove any duplicates
sqllab_gross_clean <- sqllab_gross_clean %>% 
  distinct(.keep_all = TRUE)

# Check the dimensions of the Gross dataset after removing duplicates
dim(sqllab_gross_clean)
#> [1] 135420     11

There are no duplicate data in the Gross dataset

sqllab_external_clean <- sqllab_external %>% 
  
  mutate(
    # Changing data types
    cut_off_date= ymd(cut_off_date),

    area = as.factor(area), 
    branch = as.factor(branch), 
    bucket = as.factor(bucket),
    noa = as.integer(noa),
    outstanding_amount = as.numeric(outstanding_amount),
    
    # adding new column
    date = day(cut_off_date),
    month = month(cut_off_date),
    year = year(cut_off_date)
  ) %>% 
  
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date))

TAB 1 (NPL OVERVIEW)

In this NPL Overview, the analysis focuses on identifying the total outstanding amount for each island by aggregating the outstanding amounts across all buckets for every island and each specific reporting date.

The dashboard also compares weekly NPL performance across islands using three different NPL coverage levels: External, Net, and Gross.

  • NPL External: includes only the external portion of non-performing loans.
  • NPL Net: includes the external portion along with eligible claim insurance coverage.
  • NPL Gross: provides the broadest coverage by including NPL Net and additional non-performing loan exposure, including write-offs (+WO).

Line 1 (Overview Gross)

Now, I’m going to wrangle the data to capture only the total outstanding amount for each island, comparing the values between last week and this week.

# Data Wrangling
gross_total_outstanding <- sqllab_gross_clean %>%
  filter(cut_off_date <= "2025-11-01") %>% 
  group_by(cut_off_date, island) %>% 
  summarise(total_outstanding_amount= sum(outstanding_amount)) %>%
  ungroup() %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date)) %>% 
  mutate(
    Date = factor(
      format(cut_off_date, "%d %b %Y"),
      levels = format(sort(unique(cut_off_date)),"%d %b %Y"))
  ) %>% 
  head(14) # this and last week

           aes(fill = Date)) +

                                           suffix = "B",
                                           accuracy = 1)) +
  geom_text(aes(y = total_outstanding_amount + 1.5e10,
                label = format(floor(total_outstanding_amount/1e8)/10,
                                     big.mark = ".",
                                     decimal.mark = ","),
                group = Date),
            position = position_dodge(width = 1),
            size = 2.8) +
  scale_fill_manual(values= c("lavender","purple")) +
  labs(title = "Weekly Gross Total Outstanding",
       subtitle = "in billion Rupiah", 
       x = "Island",
       y = "Total Outstanding",
       fill = "Date") +
  theme_minimal() +
  theme(legend.position = "bottom")

#> Levels: 01. Current 02. 1-30 DPD 03. 31-60 DPD 04. 61-90 DPD 05. 90+ DPD

There are 5 bucket category in the “Gross” dataset.

In order to obtain the NPL value, we first need to calculate the ratio between the total outstanding amount in the “DPD 90+” bucket and the overall total outstanding amount for each cut-off date and island.

The Non-Performing Loan (NPL) ratio can be calculated as:
\[ \text{NPL} = \frac{\text{Total Outstanding Amount (DPD 90+)}}{\text{Total Outstanding Amount (All Buckets)}} \]

To begin, we’ll calculate the total outstanding amount for loans in the 05. 90+ DPD bucket, summarized by cut-off date and island.

# Data Wrangling
# Total amount DPD 90+
gross_DPD_90 <- sqllab_gross_clean %>%
  filter(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD") %>% 
  group_by(cut_off_date, island) %>% 
  summarise(DPD_90 = sum(outstanding_amount)) %>%
  ungroup() %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date)) %>% 
  mutate(
    date = day(cut_off_date)
  )

gross_DPD_90

#>  3 2025-11-01   Kalimantan           47065999364.     1

Next, we’ll calculate the total outstanding amount for each cut-off date and island across all DPD buckets.

# Data Wrangling 2
# Total Outstanding 2
gross_total_outstanding2 <- sqllab_gross_clean %>%
  group_by(cut_off_date, island) %>% 
  summarise(total_outstanding_amount= sum(outstanding_amount)) %>%
  ungroup() %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date)) %>% 
  mutate(
    date = day(cut_off_date)
  )

Next, we’ll merge the datasets containing the DPD 90+ outstanding amount and the total outstanding amount into a single dataframe, allowing us to calculate the NPL ratio for each cut-off date and island.

# Merge DPD 90+ outstanding amount with total outstanding amount to calculate current NPL
gross_NPL_Current <- gross_DPD_90 %>% 
  inner_join(gross_total_outstanding2, by = c("cut_off_date", "island")) %>% 
  mutate(
    NPL = round((DPD_90 / total_outstanding_amount * 100),2),
    Date = factor(
      format(cut_off_date, "%d %b %Y"),
      levels = format(sort(unique(cut_off_date)),"%d %b %Y"))
  ) %>%
  select (-c(date.x, date.y)) %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date)) %>%
  filter(cut_off_date <= "2025-11-01") %>% 
  head(14) # this and last week

This bar chart illustrates the weekly change in NPL (Non-Performing Loan) Gross percentage across Indonesia’s islands for 25 October 2025 and 01 November 2025. The visualization captures how the credit quality shifts regionally over time.

  • Papua records the highest NPL levels, increasing slightly from 20.50% to 22.80%.
  • Maluku also shows a noticeable rise, moving from 20.18% to 22.33%.
  • Kalimantan stands out with the biggest decline from 21.35% to 18.12%, suggesting improved credit performance.

unique(sqllab_net_clean$bucket)
#> [1] 01. Current   02. 1-30 DPD  03. 31-60 DPD 04. 61-90 DPD 05. 90+ DPD  
#> Levels: 01. Current 02. 1-30 DPD 03. 31-60 DPD 04. 61-90 DPD 05. 90+ DPD

There are 5 bucket category in the “Net” dataset. Just like the Gross NPL plot, we now need to calculate the Net NPL by obtaining the total outstanding amount in the “DPD 90+” bucket and the overall total outstanding amount for each cut-off date and island.

The key difference between NPL Gross and NPL Net is that the latter excludes Write-Off (WO) values. These values will then be used to derive the Net NPL percentage.

# Data Wrangling
# Total amount DPD 90+
net_DPD_90 <- sqllab_net_clean %>%
  filter(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD") %>% 
  group_by(cut_off_date, island) %>% 
  summarise(DPD_90 = sum(outstanding_amount)) %>%
  ungroup() %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date)) %>% 
  mutate(
    date = day(cut_off_date)
  )

#> Levels: 01. Current 02. 1-30 DPD 03. 31-60 DPD 04. 61-90 DPD 05. 90+ DPD

There are 5 bucket category in the “External” dataset.

We now need to calculate the External NPL by obtaining the total outstanding amount in the “DPD 90+” bucket and the overall total outstanding amount for each cut-off date and island.

The main distinction between NPL Gross and NPL External is that the latter excludes both Write-Off (WO) values and Eligible Claim Insurance. These figures will then be used to derive the External NPL percentage.

# Data Wrangling
# Total amount DPD 90+
external_DPD_90 <- sqllab_external_clean %>%
  filter(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD") %>% 
  group_by(cut_off_date, island) %>% 
  summarise(DPD_90 = sum(outstanding_amount)) %>%
  ungroup() %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date)) %>% 
  mutate(
    date = day(cut_off_date)
  )

external_DPD_90

#>  2 2025-11-01   Jawa                 4678951964.     1

# Data Wrangling 2
# Total Outstanding 2
external_total_outstanding2 <- sqllab_external_clean %>%
  group_by(cut_off_date, island) %>% 
  summarise(total_outstanding_amount= sum(outstanding_amount)) %>%
  ungroup() %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date)) %>% 
  mutate(
    date = day(cut_off_date)
  )

external_total_outstanding2
#> # A tibble: 427 × 4
#>    cut_off_date island               total_outstanding_amount  date
#>    <date>       <fct>                                   <dbl> <int>
#>  1 2025-11-01   Bali & Nusa Tenggara             71226252420.     1
#>  2 2025-11-01   Jawa                            156117687350.     1
#>  3 2025-11-01   Kalimantan                      135307784341.     1
#>  4 2025-11-01   Maluku                           49013872412.     1
#>  5 2025-11-01   Papua                           120467879306.     1
#>  6 2025-11-01   Sulawesi                        151287046551.     1
#>  7 2025-11-01   Sumatera                        245719756420.     1
#>  8 2025-10-25   Bali & Nusa Tenggara             79929170711.    25
#>  9 2025-10-25   Jawa                            149145882346.    25
#> 10 2025-10-25   Kalimantan                      127755024506.    25
#> # ℹ 417 more rows
# Merge DPD 90+ outstanding amount with total outstanding amount to calculate current NPL
external_NPL_Current <- external_DPD_90 %>% 
  inner_join(external_total_outstanding2, by = c("cut_off_date", "island")) %>% 
  mutate(
    NPL = round((DPD_90 / total_outstanding_amount * 100),2),
    Date = factor(
      format(cut_off_date, "%d %b %Y"),
      levels = format(sort(unique(cut_off_date)),"%d %b %Y"))
  ) %>%
  select (-c(date.x, date.y)) %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date)) %>%
  filter(cut_off_date <= "2025-11-01") %>% 
  head(14) # this and last week

In this step, the Gross, Net, and External NPL datasets are combined and aggregated at the national level based on each cut-off date. The total outstanding amounts and DPD 90+ values are calculated to derive the respective NPL percentages for each type.

This processed data will then be used to visualize the Weekly National NPL Comparison by Type, showing how each NPL category evolves over time.

# Data Wrangling ~> Nationally
GNE_NPL_current <- gross_NPL_Current %>% 
  
  # Merging all current NPL datasets based on cut off date and island
  inner_join(net_NPL_Current, by= c("cut_off_date", "island")) %>% 
  inner_join(external_NPL_Current, by = c("cut_off_date", "island")) %>% 
  
  group_by(cut_off_date) %>% 
  summarise(
    # Aggregating/ summarizing data to national level
    DPD_90_gross = sum(DPD_90.x),
    total_outstanding_amount_gross = sum(total_outstanding_amount.x),
    DPD_90_net = sum(DPD_90.y),
    total_outstanding_amount_net = sum(total_outstanding_amount.y),
    DPD_90_external = sum(DPD_90),
    total_outstanding_amount_external = sum(total_outstanding_amount)
      ) %>% 
  ungroup() %>% 
  
  mutate(
    # NPL Gross, Net, and External
    Gross = round((DPD_90_gross / total_outstanding_amount_gross * 100),2),
    Net = round((DPD_90_net / total_outstanding_amount_net * 100),2),
    External = round((DPD_90_external / total_outstanding_amount_external * 100),2),
    
    # Date ~> for legend
    Date = factor(
      format(cut_off_date, "%d %b %Y"),
      levels = format(sort(unique(cut_off_date)),"%d %b %Y"))
  ) %>% 
  
  select(
    -c(DPD_90_gross,
       total_outstanding_amount_gross,
       DPD_90_net,
       total_outstanding_amount_net,
       DPD_90_external,
       total_outstanding_amount_external)
  )

GNE_NPL_current
#> # A tibble: 2 × 5
#>   cut_off_date Gross   Net External Date       
#>   <date>       <dbl> <dbl>    <dbl> <fct>      
#> 1 2025-10-25    20.0  10.5     2.83 25 Oct 2025
#> 2 2025-11-01    20.4  10.7     2.82 01 Nov 2025
# pivot longer
GNE_NPL_current <- GNE_NPL_current %>% 
  pivot_longer(
    cols = c(Gross, Net, External),
    names_to = "NPL_type",
    values_to = "NPL"
  ) %>% 
  mutate(NPL_type = factor(NPL_type, levels = c("Gross", "Net", "External")))

GNE_NPL_current <- GNE_NPL_current %>%

    label = glue(
      "NPL: {number(NPL,  big.mark = '.', decimal.mark = ',', accuracy = 0.01)}%
      Cut Off Date: {format(as.Date(cut_off_date), '%d %b %Y')}"
    )
  )

# PLOT 1.4: Weekly National NPL Comparison by Type
plot1.4 <- ggplot(GNE_NPL_current, aes(x = NPL_type, 
                    y = NPL,
                    text = label)) +
  
  geom_col(position = position_dodge(width = 0.9),
           aes(fill = Date)) +
  geom_text(aes(y = NPL + 1.4,
                label = label_number(big.mark = ".",
                                     decimal.mark = ",", 
                                     accuracy = 0.01)
                (NPL),
                group = Date),
            position = position_dodge(width = 1),
            size = 3.0) +
  scale_fill_manual(values= c("lavender", "purple")) +
  labs(title = "Weekly National NPL Comparison by Type",
       x = "NPL Types",
       y = "NPL (%)") +
  theme_minimal() +
  theme(legend.position = "bottom")

plot1.4

# This is for interactive plot
# ggplotly(plot1.4, tooltip = "text") %>% 
#   layout(legend = list(orientation = "h",
#                        y = -0.3))

The chart above shows the Weekly National NPL Comparison by Type, comparing data from 25 Oct 2025 and 01 Nov 2025.

  • Overall, Gross and Net NPL slightly increased from 19.95% to 20.39% and 10.49% to 10.72%, respectively, indicating a minor rise in national non-performing loans.
  • Meanwhile, External NPL remained stable at around 2.8%, suggesting consistent performance in externally financed loans.

By definition, Gross NPL will always be higher than Net NPL, and Net NPL will always be higher than External NPL. This is because Net NPL excludes loans that have been written off, while External NPL further excludes loans covered by eligible claim assurances.

Now, we need to aggregate the Net NPL data on a weekly basis by summing the DPD 90+ and total outstanding amounts for each cut-off date.

The weekly Net NPL percentage is then calculated, rounded to two decimal places, and arranged chronologically to prepare for visualization.

# Data Wrangling
net_NPL_weekly_comparison <- net_NPL_Current %>% 
  group_by(cut_off_date) %>% 
  summarise(NPL_weekly = (sum(DPD_90)/sum(total_outstanding_amount))*100) %>%
  ungroup() %>% 
  mutate(
    NPL_weekly = round(NPL_weekly,2),
    Date = factor(
      format(cut_off_date, "%d %b %Y"),
      levels = format(sort(unique(cut_off_date)), "%d %b %Y"))
  ) %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date))

net_NPL_weekly_comparison
#> # A tibble: 2 × 3
#>   cut_off_date NPL_weekly Date       
#>   <date>            <dbl> <fct>      
#> 1 2025-11-01         10.7 01 Nov 2025
#> 2 2025-10-25         10.5 25 Oct 2025
# tooltip
net_NPL_weekly_comparison <- net_NPL_weekly_comparison %>% 
  mutate(
    label = glue(
      "NPL: {number(NPL_weekly,  big.mark = '.', decimal.mark = ',', accuracy = 0.01)}%
      Cut Off Date: {format(as.Date(cut_off_date), '%d %b %Y')}"
    )
  )

# PLOT 1.5: NPL Net Weekly Comparison
plot1.5 <- ggplot(net_NPL_weekly_comparison, aes(x = Date, 
                    y = NPL_weekly,
                    text = label)) +
  
  geom_col(position = "dodge", aes(fill = Date)) +
  scale_fill_manual(values= c("lavender", "purple")) +
  geom_text(aes(y = NPL_weekly + 0.3,
                label = label_number(big.mark = ".",
                                     decimal.mark = ",", 
                                     accuracy = 0.01)
                (NPL_weekly),
                group = Date),
            size = 3.5)  +
  labs(title = "NPL Net Weekly Comparison",
       x = "Cut Off Date",
       y = "NPL (%)") +
  theme_minimal() +
  theme(legend.position = "none")

              NPL_diff >0,
              paste0("+", format(round(NPL_diff, 2), big.mark = ".", decimal.mark = ",", nsmall = 2), "%"), # if condition
      paste0(format(round(NPL_diff, 2), big.mark = ".", decimal.mark = ",", nsmall = 2), "%") # else condition
            ))

net_Diff_DPD90_weekly
#> # A tibble: 2 × 2
#>   cut_off_date Total_DPD_90_weekly
#>   <date>                     <dbl>
#> 1 2025-11-01         131611758658.
#> 2 2025-10-25         128518958548.
# Difference Net DPD 90+ in Rp
net_Diff_DPD90_weekly <- net_Diff_DPD90_weekly %>% 
  summarise(Diff_DPD90_weekly= Total_DPD_90_weekly[1]-Total_DPD_90_weekly[2],
            Diff_DPD90_weekly = if_else(
              Diff_DPD90_weekly >0,
              paste0(" + IDR ", comma(Diff_DPD90_weekly)), # ini if-nya
              paste0(" - IDR ", comma(Diff_DPD90_weekly * (-1))) # ini else-nya
            ),
            
            Diff_DPD90_weekly = gsub(",", ".", Diff_DPD90_weekly),  # change thousand sep to "."
    Diff_DPD90_weekly = sub("\\.(\\d{2})$", ",\\1", Diff_DPD90_weekly) # change decimal sep to ","
    ) 

net_Diff_DPD90_weekly
#> # A tibble: 1 × 1
#>   Diff_DPD90_weekly     
#>   <chr>                 
#> 1 " + IDR 3.092.800.111"

Now, we’re going to calculate the Gross NPL value for each island across every cut-off date.

# Data Wrangling: Gross NPL for each island & cut off date
gross_NPL_last_8_weeks <- gross_DPD_90 %>% 
  inner_join(gross_total_outstanding2, by = c("cut_off_date", "island")) %>% 
  mutate(
    Gross = round((DPD_90 / total_outstanding_amount * 100),2),
    Date = factor(
      format(cut_off_date, "%d %b %Y"),
      levels = format(sort(unique(cut_off_date)),"%d %b %Y"))
  ) %>%
  select (-c(date.x, date.y)) %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date)) %>%
  filter(cut_off_date <= "2025-11-01")

After obtaining each island and cut-off date’s Gross NPL value, we now calculate the overall national Gross NPL by grouping the data based on the cut-off date, then summing all DPD 90+ values and dividing them by the total outstanding amounts. This process results in the national Gross NPL value for each cut-off date.

# National Gross NPL value for each cut off date
gross_NPL_last_8_weeks <- gross_NPL_last_8_weeks %>%
  group_by(cut_off_date) %>% 
  summarise(Gross= round((sum(DPD_90)/sum(total_outstanding_amount)*100),2)) %>%
  ungroup() %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date))

Next, it’s time to pivot the dataset to make it easier to visualize.

Since we only want to focus on the national NPL data for the last 8 weeks, we will keep only the top 24 observations, representing 3 NPL types × 8 weeks = 24 data points.

# Pivot and taking the last 8 weeks national NPL values
GNE_NPL_last_8_weeks <- GNE_NPL_last_8_weeks %>% 
  pivot_longer(
    cols = c(Gross, Net, External),
    names_to = "NPL_type",
    values_to = "NPL"
  ) %>% 
  mutate(NPL_type = factor(NPL_type, levels = c("Gross", "Net", "External"))) %>% 
  head(24)

    breaks = GNE_NPL_last_8_weeks$cut_off_date, 
    date_labels = "%b %d"
  ) +
  scale_y_continuous(
    limits = c(0, max(GNE_NPL_last_8_weeks$NPL) + 10),
    breaks = seq(0,100,5)
  ) +
  scale_color_manual(values = c(
    "Gross" = "darkgreen",
    "Net" = "red",
    "External" = "blue"),
    name = NULL) +
  labs(title = "Last 8 Weeks NPL Position by Type",
       x = "Cut Off Date",
       y = "NPL (%)",
       color = "NPL Type") +
  theme_minimal() +
  theme(legend.position = "bottom")

The chart presents the NPL trend over the last 8 weeks, separated by Gross, Net, and External types.

  • Gross NPL remained relatively stable, fluctuating slightly between 19.01% and 20.88%, ending at 20.39% on 1 November 2025.
  • Net NPL showed minor variation, with a low of 9.89% and peaking at 10.96%, finishing at 10.72%.
  • External NPL stayed consistently low, ranging from 2.58% to 2.87%, ending at 2.82%.

Overall, the NPL levels remained steady across all types, with Net and Gross NPL showing a slight upward movement toward the end of the period.

The same as the previous step, firstly, we’re going to calculate the Gross NPL value for each island across every cut-off date.

# Data Wrangling: Gross NPL for each island & cut off date
gross_NPL_last_4_months <- gross_DPD_90 %>% 
  inner_join(gross_total_outstanding2, by = c("cut_off_date", "island")) %>% 
  mutate(
    Gross = round((DPD_90 / total_outstanding_amount * 100),2),
    Date = factor(
      format(cut_off_date, "%d %b %Y"),
      levels = format(sort(unique(cut_off_date)),"%d %b %Y"))
  ) %>%
  select (-c(date.x, date.y)) %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date)) %>%
  filter(cut_off_date <= "2025-11-01")

We also need to merge all the Gross, Net, and External NPL values into a single dataset to make it neater for the next step.

# Merging Gross, Net, and External national NPL values into one dataset
GNE_NPL_last_4_months <- gross_NPL_last_4_months %>%

Now, we want to obtain the national NPL values for the last 4 months.

To take the NPL values from the last cut-off date of each month, we first need to add separate columns for date, month, and year based on the existing cut-off date.

# Adding date, month, and year column
GNE_NPL_last_4_months <- GNE_NPL_last_4_months %>% 
  mutate(
    date = day(cut_off_date),
    month = floor_date(cut_off_date, "month"),
    year = year(cut_off_date)
    ) %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date))

GNE_NPL_last_4_months <- GNE_NPL_last_4_months %>%
  group_by(month) %>% 
  filter(cut_off_date <= "2025-11-01") %>%

  head(4)

# Pivot and adding NPL type column 
GNE_NPL_last_4_months <- GNE_NPL_last_4_months %>% 
  pivot_longer(
    cols = c(Gross, Net, External),
    names_to = "NPL_type",

  ) %>% 
  mutate(NPL_type = factor(NPL_type, levels = c("Gross", "Net", "External")))

The chart illustrates the NPL trend over the past 4 months for Gross, Net, and External portfolios.

  • Gross NPL remained relatively stable, moving slightly from 20.22% (Aug 30) to 20.39% (Nov 1).
  • Net NPL showed a mild decline from 10.70% in August to 10.49% in September, before rising again to 10.72% in November.
  • External NPL stayed consistently low and stable, ranging narrowly between 2.75% and 2.84%.

Overall, Gross and Net NPLs indicate minor fluctuations but no significant changes, suggesting portfolio quality remained steady throughout the observed period.

# Data Wrangling: Gross NPL for each island & cut off date
gross_NPL_last_4_quartals <- gross_DPD_90 %>% 
  inner_join(gross_total_outstanding2, by = c("cut_off_date", "island")) %>% 
  mutate(
    Gross = round((DPD_90 / total_outstanding_amount * 100),2),
    Date = factor(
      format(cut_off_date, "%d %b %Y"),
      levels = format(sort(unique(cut_off_date)),"%d %b %Y"))
  ) %>%
  select (-c(date.x, date.y)) %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date)) %>%
  filter(cut_off_date <= "2025-11-01")

To identify the quarter of each cut-off date, we’ll create a function that labels it according to its month.

# Function to determine Q1–Q4: Quarter
quartal <- function(x)
  {
  if(x == 3)
    {
    z <- "Q1" # returns "Q1" if the value of x is 3 (March)
    }
  else if(x == 6)
    {
    z <- "Q2" # returns "Q2" if the value of x is 6 (June)
    }
  else if(x == 9)
    {
    z <- "Q3" # returns "Q3" if the value of x is 9 (September)
    }
  else
    {
    z <- "Q4" # returns "Q4" if the value of x is 12 (December)
    }
  }
# Example: trying out the "quartal" function above
print(quartal(6))
#> [1] "Q2"

When the input value is 6 (June), the function correctly returns Q2, which represents the second quarter.

Now, we need to apply the Quartal function to identify which quarter each cut-off date belongs to. We will then filter the dataset to include only the months March (3), June (6), September (9), and December (12) to ensure that only the end-of-quarter data is used.

We also want to make sure to include only the maximum date of each quarter and take only the most recent year, ensuring that we are using the latest available quarterly data.

# Applying the Quartal function to extract only the most recent date from each quarter
GNE_NPL_last_4_quartals <- GNE_NPL_last_4_quartals %>% 
  mutate(
    month_num = month(cut_off_date),
    quartal = sapply(month_num, quartal)
  ) %>% 
  filter(cut_off_date <= "2025-11-01") %>% 
  filter(
    month_num %in% c("3", "6", "9", "12"),
  ) %>% 
  group_by(quartal) %>% 
  filter(year == max(year)) %>% 
  group_by(month_num) %>% 
  filter(date == max(date)) %>% 
  ungroup() %>% 
  arrange(desc(cut_off_date))

GNE_NPL_last_4_quartals
#> # A tibble: 4 × 10
#>   cut_off_date Gross   Net External Date         date month       year month_num
#>   <date>       <dbl> <dbl>    <dbl> <fct>       <int> <date>     <dbl>     <dbl>
#> 1 2025-09-27    20.1  10.5     2.84 27 Sep 2025    27 2025-09-01  2025         9
#> 2 2025-06-28    20.5  10.7     2.85 28 Jun 2025    28 2025-06-01  2025         6
#> 3 2025-03-29    20.1  10.4     2.79 29 Mar 2025    29 2025-03-01  2025         3
#> 4 2024-12-28    19.6  10.2     2.68 28 Dec 2024    28 2024-12-01  2024        12

# Pivot and adding NPL type column 
GNE_NPL_last_4_quartals <- GNE_NPL_last_4_quartals %>% 
  pivot_longer(
    cols = c(Gross, Net, External),
    names_to = "NPL_type",
    values_to = "NPL"
  ) %>% 
  mutate(NPL_type = factor(NPL_type, levels = c("Gross", "Net", "External")))

                                     accuracy = 0.01)
                (NPL)),
            size = 3) +
  scale_y_continuous(
    limits = c(0, max(GNE_NPL_last_4_quartals$NPL) + 10),
    breaks = seq(0,100,5)
  ) +
  scale_color_manual(values = c(
    "Gross" = "darkgreen",
    "Net" = "red",
    "External" = "blue"),
    name = NULL) +
  labs(title = "Last 4 Quartals NPL Position by Type",
       x = "Cut Off Date",
       y = "NPL (%)",
       color = "NPL Type") +
  theme_minimal() +
  theme(legend.position = "bottom")

The chart presents the NPL trend over the last four quartals, comparing Gross, Net, and External NPL ratios.

  • Gross NPL shows a gradual increase from 19.64% (Q4) to 20.49% (Q2) before slightly easing to 20.11% (Q3), indicating a generally stable performance across the period.
  • Net NPL rose from 10.23% in Q4 to 10.70% in Q2, followed by a marginal decline to 10.49% in Q3, reflecting minor fluctuation but consistent control of credit quality.
  • External NPL remained very stable, moving slightly from 2.68% to 2.85%, then closing at 2.84%, suggesting strong management of external exposures.

Overall, all three NPL categories maintained steady positions, with only slight movements across the quartals—implying consistent portfolio quality and controlled risk levels.

TAB 2 (DPD BUCKET OVERVIEW)

Section 1 (DPD Bucket by Amount)

Now, I’m going to create bar plots to visualize the total outstanding amount across islands for each DPD bucket. These visualizations provide a clearer overview of outstanding loan distribution within the Gross, Net, and External datasets, making the comparison across islands and bucket categories easier to interpret.

The main goals of these plots are to:

  • Compare the total outstanding amount across Gross, Net, and External datasets.
  • Identify which islands have the highest and lowest outstanding amounts within each DPD bucket.
  • Analyze the distribution of outstanding balances across islands and bucket categories.
  • Highlight the DPD 90+ bucket to identify islands with higher levels of overdue or unpaid loans.

Now, we’re going to derive the latest outstanding amount from the gross dataset, specifically for the “02. 1–30 DPD” bucket in each island.

# Gross: Outstanding amount for "02. DPD 1-30" bucket
DPD_bucket_by_amount02_gross <- sqllab_gross_clean %>% 
  filter(bucket == "02. 1-30 DPD",
         cut_off_date == "2025-11-01") %>% 
  group_by(island) %>% 
  summarise(outstanding_amount = sum(outstanding_amount)) %>% 
  ungroup()

After obtaining the latest Gross, Net, and External outstanding amounts, specifically for the “02. 1–30 DPD” bucket in each island, we’re going to merge and pivot them into one dataset for easier visualization.

# Merging Gross, Net, and External "02. DPD 1-30" bucket outstanding amounts into one dataset
DPD_bucket_by_amount02 <- DPD_bucket_by_amount02_gross %>% 
  inner_join(DPD_bucket_by_amount02_net, by = "island") %>% 
  inner_join(DPD_bucket_by_amount02_external, by = "island") %>% 
  rename(
    Gross = outstanding_amount.x,
    Net = outstanding_amount.y,
    External = outstanding_amount
  )

The chart shows the total outstanding DPD 1–30 (in billion Rupiah) across different islands, comparing Gross, Net, and External figures.

  • Sumatera recorded the highest exposure, with Gross 92.9B, Net 71.1B, and External 58.4B, indicating the largest loan volume in early delinquency.
  • Jawa and Sulawesi followed, showing Gross 56.1B and 55.3B respectively, suggesting significant portfolio size but still well-managed within the early DPD category.
  • Kalimantan and Papua maintained moderate levels, with Gross around 50.6B and 45.4B, while Bali & Nusa Tenggara and Maluku reported relatively lower exposures.

Overall, the Gross DPD 1–30 remains consistently higher than Net and External across all islands, reflecting expected write-off and collection adjustments in later stages.

Like the previous example, we’re now going to merge and pivot the data into a single dataset for easier visualization.

# Merging Gross, Net, and External "03. DPD 31-60" bucket outstanding amounts into one dataset
DPD_bucket_by_amount03 <- DPD_bucket_by_amount03_gross %>% 
  inner_join(DPD_bucket_by_amount03_net, by = "island") %>% 
  inner_join(DPD_bucket_by_amount03_external, by = "island") %>% 
  rename(
    Gross = outstanding_amount.x,
    Net = outstanding_amount.y,
    External = outstanding_amount
  )

DPD_bucket_by_amount03
#> # A tibble: 7 × 4
#>   island                      Gross          Net     External
#>   <fct>                       <dbl>        <dbl>        <dbl>
#> 1 Bali & Nusa Tenggara 23901801836. 17753080908. 14261813358.
#> 2 Jawa                 53514956086. 41069456228. 34781958403.
#> 3 Kalimantan           52384108110. 39070205962. 31718571037.
#> 4 Maluku               16380364361. 11955745329. 10212794139.
#> 5 Papua                42443492863. 32300294975. 26677463004.
#> 6 Sulawesi             60825038183. 45829473488. 37493818108.
#> 7 Sumatera             93988750331. 69826052554. 57419784697.
# Pivot and adding NPL type column 
DPD_bucket_by_amount03 <- DPD_bucket_by_amount03 %>%
  pivot_longer(
    cols = c(Gross, Net, External),
    names_to = "Type",
    values_to = "Total_OS"
  ) %>% 
  mutate(Type = factor(Type, levels = c("Gross", "Net", "External")))
  
DPD_bucket_by_amount03
#> # A tibble: 21 × 3
#>    island               Type         Total_OS
#>    <fct>                <fct>           <dbl>
#>  1 Bali & Nusa Tenggara Gross    23901801836.
#>  2 Bali & Nusa Tenggara Net      17753080908.
#>  3 Bali & Nusa Tenggara External 14261813358.
#>  4 Jawa                 Gross    53514956086.
#>  5 Jawa                 Net      41069456228.
#>  6 Jawa                 External 34781958403.
#>  7 Kalimantan           Gross    52384108110.
#>  8 Kalimantan           Net      39070205962.
#>  9 Kalimantan           External 31718571037.
#> 10 Maluku               Gross    16380364361.
#> # ℹ 11 more rows
# tooltip
DPD_bucket_by_amount03 <- DPD_bucket_by_amount03 %>%
  mutate(
    label = glue(
      "Total Oustanding:IDR {number(Total_OS, big.mark = '.', decimal.mark = ',', accuracy = 1)}"
    )
  )

DPD_bucket_by_amount03
#> # A tibble: 21 × 4
#>    island               Type         Total_OS label                             
#>    <fct>                <fct>           <dbl> <glue>                            
#>  1 Bali & Nusa Tenggara Gross    23901801836. Total Oustanding:IDR 23.901.801.8…
#>  2 Bali & Nusa Tenggara Net      17753080908. Total Oustanding:IDR 17.753.080.9…
#>  3 Bali & Nusa Tenggara External 14261813358. Total Oustanding:IDR 14.261.813.3…
#>  4 Jawa                 Gross    53514956086. Total Oustanding:IDR 53.514.956.0…
#>  5 Jawa                 Net      41069456228. Total Oustanding:IDR 41.069.456.2…
#>  6 Jawa                 External 34781958403. Total Oustanding:IDR 34.781.958.4…
#>  7 Kalimantan           Gross    52384108110. Total Oustanding:IDR 52.384.108.1…
#>  8 Kalimantan           Net      39070205962. Total Oustanding:IDR 39.070.205.9…
#>  9 Kalimantan           External 31718571037. Total Oustanding:IDR 31.718.571.0…
#> 10 Maluku               Gross    16380364361. Total Oustanding:IDR 16.380.364.3…
#> # ℹ 11 more rows
# PLOT 2.2: DPD Bucket by Amount (03. 31-60 DPD)
plot2.2 <- ggplot(DPD_bucket_by_amount03, aes(x = island, 
                    y = Total_OS,
                    text = label)) +
  
  geom_col(position = position_dodge(width = 0.9),
           aes(fill = Type)) +
  geom_text(aes(y = Total_OS + 2.5e9,
                label = format(floor(Total_OS/1e8)/10,
                                     big.mark = ".",
                                     decimal.mark = ","),
                group = Type),
            position = position_dodge(width = 1),
            size = 3) +
  scale_y_continuous(labels = label_number(scale = 1e-9, 
                                           suffix = "B", 
                                           accuracy = 1)) +
   scale_fill_manual(values = c("darkgreen", "red","blue"),
                    name = NULL) +
  labs(title = "DPD 31-60",
       x = "Island",
       y = "Total Outstanding") +
  theme_minimal() +
  theme(legend.position = "bottom")

plot2.2

# This is for interactive plot
# ggplotly(plot2.2, tooltip = "text") %>% 
#   layout(title = list(text = paste0(
#       "DPD 31-60",
#       "<br><sup>in billion Rupiah</sup>")),
#       legend = list(orientation = "h",
#                     y = -0.3))

The chart shows Total Outstanding (in billion Rupiah) for DPD 31–60 across different islands in Indonesia, categorized into Gross, Net, and External values.

  • Sumatera has the highest outstanding amounts across all categories, reaching 93.9B Gross, 69.8B Net, and 57.4B External.
  • Jawa and Sulawesi follow with relatively high totals, while Maluku records the lowest with 16.3B Gross.
  • Across all islands, Gross values consistently exceed Net and External, indicating deductions or adjustments between categories.
  • Overall, the data suggests a concentration of higher DPD 31–60 exposures in Sumatera, Jawa, and Sulawesi regions.

Lastly, for the DPD bucket by amount section, we’re going to derive the latest outstanding amount from the gross, net, and external dataset, specifically for the last bucket, “05. 90+ DPD”, in each island.

# Gross: Outstanding amount for "05. 90+ DPD" bucket
DPD_bucket_by_amount05_gross <- sqllab_gross_clean %>% 
  filter(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD",
         cut_off_date == "2025-11-01") %>% 
  group_by(island) %>% 
  summarise(outstanding_amount = sum(outstanding_amount)) %>% 
  ungroup()

After obtaining the latest Gross, Net, and External outstanding amounts, specifically for the last bucket, “05. 90+ DPD” bucket in each island, we’re going to merge and pivot them into one dataset for easier visualization.

# Merging Gross, Net, and External "05. 90+ DPD" bucket outstanding amounts into one dataset
DPD_bucket_by_amount05 <- DPD_bucket_by_amount05_gross %>% 
  inner_join(DPD_bucket_by_amount05_net, by = "island") %>% 
  inner_join(DPD_bucket_by_amount05_external, by = "island") %>% 
  rename(
    Gross = outstanding_amount.x,
    Net = outstanding_amount.y,
    External = outstanding_amount
  )

DPD_bucket_by_amount05
#> # A tibble: 7 × 4
#>   island                      Gross          Net    External
#>   <fct>                       <dbl>        <dbl>       <dbl>
#> 1 Bali & Nusa Tenggara 31003030413. 10962829834. 2306183060.
#> 2 Jawa                 64124530442. 22503499617. 4678951964.
#> 3 Kalimantan           47065999364. 15959716160. 3150806736.
#> 4 Maluku               21402843091.  7596672396. 1435651017.
#> 5 Papua                55714241579. 18630620970. 3649461770.
#> 6 Sulawesi             56068920845. 20494808363. 4164370184.
#> 7 Sumatera             97924116601. 35463611319. 6808339308.
# Pivot and adding NPL type column 
DPD_bucket_by_amount05 <- DPD_bucket_by_amount05 %>%
  pivot_longer(
    cols = c(Gross, Net, External),
    names_to = "Type",
    values_to = "Total_OS"
  ) %>% 
  mutate(Type = factor(Type, levels = c("Gross", "Net", "External")))
  
DPD_bucket_by_amount05

#>  9 Kalimantan           External  3150806736.
#> 10 Maluku               Gross    21402843091.

# tooltip
DPD_bucket_by_amount05 <- DPD_bucket_by_amount05 %>%
  mutate(
    label = glue(
      "Total Oustanding:IDR {number(Total_OS, big.mark = '.', decimal.mark = ',', accuracy = 1)}"
    )
  )

#> # ℹ 11 more rows
# PLOT 2.4: DPD Bucket by Amount (05. 90+ DPD)
plot2.4 <- ggplot(DPD_bucket_by_amount05, aes(x = island, 
                    y = Total_OS,
                    text = label)) +
  
  geom_col(position = position_dodge(width = 0.9),
           aes(fill = Type)) +
  geom_text(aes(y = Total_OS + 2.5e9,
                label = format(floor(Total_OS/1e8)/10,
                                     big.mark = ".",
                                     decimal.mark = ","),
                group = Type),
            position = position_dodge(width = 0.9),
            size = 3) +
  scale_y_continuous(labels = label_number(scale = 1e-9, 
                                           suffix = "B", 
                                           accuracy = 1)) +
   scale_fill_manual(values = c("darkgreen", "red","blue"),
                    name = NULL) +
  labs(title = "DPD 90+",
       x = "Island",
       y = "Total Outstanding") +
  theme_minimal() +
  theme(legend.position = "bottom")

plot2.4

# This is for interactive plot
# ggplotly(plot2.4, tooltip = "text") %>% 
#   layout(title = list(text = paste0(
#       "DPD 90+",
#       "<br><sup>in billion Rupiah</sup>")),
#       legend = list(orientation = "h",
#                     y = -0.3))

The chart presents Total Outstanding (in billion Rupiah) for DPD 90+ across several islands in Indonesia, categorized into Gross, Net, and External amounts.

  • Sumatera records the highest figures, reaching 97.9B Gross, 35.4B Net, and 6.8B External.
  • Jawa, Sulawesi, and Papua also show substantial levels, particularly in the Gross category.
  • Maluku and Bali & Nusa Tenggara maintain relatively lower totals, with Gross values under 35B.
  • The Gross values remain significantly higher than Net and External across all islands, indicating a notable gap due to risk provisions or write-offs.
  • Overall, Sumatera continues to dominate outstanding amounts in DPD 90+, consistent with earlier DPD bands.

Section 2 (DPD Bucket by Accounts)

Now, I’m going to create a similar set of bar plots to visualize the total number of accounts (NOA) across islands for each DPD bucket. These visualizations provide a clearer overview of accounts distribution within the Gross, Net, and External datasets, making it easier to compare the concentration of accounts across islands and bucket categories.

The main goals of these plots are to:

  • Compare the total number of accounts (NOA) across Gross, Net, and External datasets.
  • Identify which islands have the highest and lowest number of accounts within each DPD bucket.
  • Analyze the distribution of accounts across islands and bucket categories.
  • Highlight the DPD 90+ bucket to identify islands that require more attention due to having higher numbers of overdue accounts.

Now, we’re going to derive the latest NOA (Number of accounts) from the gross, net, and external dataset, specifically for the “03. 31-60 DPD” bucket in each island.

# Gross: NOA for "03. 31-60 DPD" bucket
DPD_bucket_by_accounts03_gross <- sqllab_gross_clean %>% 
  filter(bucket == "03. 31-60 DPD",
         cut_off_date == "2025-11-01") %>% 
  group_by(island) %>% 
  summarise(total_noa = sum(noa)) %>% 
  ungroup()

DPD_bucket_by_accounts03_gross

#>   island               total_noa

#> 3 Kalimantan               18053
#> 4 Maluku                    5690
#> 5 Papua                    14883
#> 6 Sulawesi                 20514
#> 7 Sumatera                 32491
# Net: NOA for "03. 31-60 DPD" bucket
DPD_bucket_by_accounts03_net <- sqllab_net_clean %>% 
  filter(bucket == "03. 31-60 DPD",
         cut_off_date == "2025-11-01") %>% 
  group_by(island) %>% 
  summarise(total_noa = sum(noa))%>% 
  ungroup()

# External: NOA for "03. 31-60 DPD" bucket
DPD_bucket_by_accounts03_external <- sqllab_external_clean %>%

         cut_off_date == "2025-11-01") %>% 
  group_by(island) %>% 
  summarise(total_noa = sum(noa)) %>%

We then merge and pivot all the latest Gross, Net, and External NOA into one dataset for easier visualization.

# Merging Gross, Net, and External "03. 31-60 DPD" bucket NOA into one dataset
DPD_bucket_by_accounts03 <- DPD_bucket_by_accounts03_gross %>% 
  inner_join(DPD_bucket_by_accounts03_net, by = "island") %>% 
  inner_join(DPD_bucket_by_accounts03_external, by = "island") %>% 
  rename(
    Gross = total_noa.x,
    Net = total_noa.y,
    External = total_noa
  )

DPD_bucket_by_accounts03
#> # A tibble: 7 × 4
#>   island               Gross   Net External
#>   <fct>                <int> <int>    <int>
#> 1 Bali & Nusa Tenggara  9998  9998     9998
#> 2 Jawa                 18446 18446    18446
#> 3 Kalimantan           18053 18053    18053
#> 4 Maluku                5690  5690     5690
#> 5 Papua                14883 14883    14883
#> 6 Sulawesi             20514 20514    20514
#> 7 Sumatera             32491 32491    32491
# Pivot and adding NPL type column 
DPD_bucket_by_accounts03 <- DPD_bucket_by_accounts03 %>%
  pivot_longer(
    cols = c(Gross, Net, External),
    names_to = "Type",
    values_to = "Total_accounts"
  ) %>% 
  mutate(Type = factor(Type, levels = c("Gross", "Net", "External")))
  
DPD_bucket_by_accounts03
#> # A tibble: 21 × 3
#>    island               Type     Total_accounts
#>    <fct>                <fct>             <int>
#>  1 Bali & Nusa Tenggara Gross              9998
#>  2 Bali & Nusa Tenggara Net                9998
#>  3 Bali & Nusa Tenggara External           9998
#>  4 Jawa                 Gross             18446
#>  5 Jawa                 Net               18446
#>  6 Jawa                 External          18446
#>  7 Kalimantan           Gross             18053
#>  8 Kalimantan           Net               18053
#>  9 Kalimantan           External          18053
#> 10 Maluku               Gross              5690
#> # ℹ 11 more rows
# tooltip
DPD_bucket_by_accounts03 <- DPD_bucket_by_accounts03 %>%
  mutate(
    label = glue(
      "Total accounts: {number(Total_accounts, big.mark = '.', decimal.mark = ',', accuracy = 1)}"
    )
  )

DPD_bucket_by_accounts03
#> # A tibble: 21 × 4
#>    island               Type     Total_accounts label

#>  2 Bali & Nusa Tenggara Net                9998 Total accounts: 9.998 
#>  3 Bali & Nusa Tenggara External           9998 Total accounts: 9.998 
#>  4 Jawa                 Gross             18446 Total accounts: 18.446
#>  5 Jawa                 Net               18446 Total accounts: 18.446
#>  6 Jawa                 External          18446 Total accounts: 18.446
#>  7 Kalimantan           Gross             18053 Total accounts: 18.053
#>  8 Kalimantan           Net               18053 Total accounts: 18.053
#>  9 Kalimantan           External          18053 Total accounts: 18.053
#> 10 Maluku               Gross              5690 Total accounts: 5.690

# PLOT 2.6: DPD Bucket by accounts (03. 31-60 DPD)
plot2.6 <- ggplot(DPD_bucket_by_accounts03, aes(x = island, 
                    y = Total_accounts,
                    text = label)) +
  
  geom_col(position = position_dodge(width = 0.9),
           aes(fill = Type)) +
  geom_text(aes(y = Total_accounts + 500,
                label = format(Total_accounts,
                               big.mark = ".",
                               decimal.mark = ","),
                group = Type),
            position = position_dodge(width = 1),
            size = 2.5) +
   scale_y_continuous(labels = label_comma(big.mark = ".", decimal.mark = ",")) +
   scale_fill_manual(values = c("darkgreen", "red","blue"),
                    name = NULL) +
  labs(title = "DPD 31-60",
       x = "Island",
       y = "Total NOA") +
  theme_minimal() +
  theme(legend.position = "bottom")

Now, we’re going to derive the latest NOA (Number of accounts) from the gross, net, and external dataset, specifically for the last bucket, “05. 90+ DPD” in each island.

# Gross: NOA for "05. 90+ DPD" bucket
DPD_bucket_by_accounts05_gross <- sqllab_gross_clean %>% 
  filter(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD",
         cut_off_date == "2025-11-01") %>% 
  group_by(island) %>% 
  summarise(total_noa = sum(noa)) %>% 
  ungroup()

         cut_off_date == "2025-11-01") %>%

We then merge and pivot all the latest Gross, Net, and External NOA into one dataset for easier visualization.

# Merging Gross, Net, and External "05. 90+ DPD" bucket NOA into one dataset
DPD_bucket_by_accounts05 <- DPD_bucket_by_accounts05_gross %>% 
  inner_join(DPD_bucket_by_accounts05_net, by = "island") %>% 
  inner_join(DPD_bucket_by_accounts05_external, by = "island") %>% 
  rename(
    Gross = total_noa.x,
    Net = total_noa.y,
    External = total_noa
  )

DPD_bucket_by_accounts05
#> # A tibble: 7 × 4
#>   island               Gross   Net External
#>   <fct>                <int> <int>    <int>
#> 1 Bali & Nusa Tenggara 10295 10295    10295
#> 2 Jawa                 21683 21683    21683
#> 3 Kalimantan           15088 15088    15088
#> 4 Maluku                7162  7162     7162
#> 5 Papua                17969 17969    17969
#> 6 Sulawesi             19032 19032    19032
#> 7 Sumatera             33241 33241    33241
# Pivot and adding NPL type column 
DPD_bucket_by_accounts05 <- DPD_bucket_by_accounts05 %>%
  pivot_longer(
    cols = c(Gross, Net, External),
    names_to = "Type",
    values_to = "Total_accounts"
  ) %>% 
  mutate(Type = factor(Type, levels = c("Gross", "Net", "External")))

                    y = Total_accounts,
                    text = label)) +
  
  geom_col(position = position_dodge(width = 0.9),
           aes(fill = Type)) +

            size = 2.5) +
   scale_y_continuous(labels = label_comma(big.mark = ".", decimal.mark = ",")) +
   scale_fill_manual(values = c("darkgreen", "red","blue"),
                    name = NULL) +
  labs(title = "DPD 90+",
       x = "Island",
       y = "Total NOA") +
  theme_minimal() +
  theme(legend.position = "bottom")

TAB 3 (NPL DETAIL)

Line 3.1 (NPL Net Detail: Island, Regional, Area, Branch)

In this section, we’re going to create a tab that displays the outstanding amount, NOA, and NPL for each DPD bucket, based on the selected cut off date, island, region, area, and branch in the dashboard.

Island

For the island level, we’re going to create two datasets: the first will display the outstanding amount, NOA, and NPL for each DPD bucket across all islands, while the second will include a specific cut-off date for more detailed analysis.

# Dataset: Net
sqllab_net_clean
#> # A tibble: 135,420 × 11
#>    cut_off_date island region area  branch bucket   noa outstanding_amount  date
#>    <date>       <fct>  <fct>  <fct> <fct>  <fct>  <int>              <dbl> <int>
#>  1 2025-11-01   Sumat… Aceh   Aceh… Aceh … 01. C…    53          76934000.     1
#>  2 2025-11-01   Sumat… Aceh   Aceh… Aceh … 02. 1…   185         218410473.     1
#>  3 2025-11-01   Sumat… Aceh   Aceh… Aceh … 03. 3…   173         317760703.     1
#>  4 2025-11-01   Sumat… Aceh   Aceh… Aceh … 04. 6…   271         811554170.     1
#>  5 2025-11-01   Sumat… Aceh   Aceh… Aceh … 05. 9…   119         271330064.     1
#>  6 2025-11-01   Sumat… Aceh   Aceh… Aceh … 01. C…   176         581834603.     1
#>  7 2025-11-01   Sumat… Aceh   Aceh… Aceh … 02. 1…   443         748995851.     1
#>  8 2025-11-01   Sumat… Aceh   Aceh… Aceh … 03. 3…   369         877552083.     1
#>  9 2025-11-01   Sumat… Aceh   Aceh… Aceh … 04. 6…   386         558000043.     1
#> 10 2025-11-01   Sumat… Aceh   Aceh… Aceh … 05. 9…   148         335235117.     1
#> # ℹ 135,410 more rows
#> # ℹ 2 more variables: month <dbl>, year <dbl>
# ISLAND: GENERAL ~> 1 input: Cut Off Date
island_general <- sqllab_net_clean %>% 
  filter(cut_off_date == "2025-11-01") %>% 
  group_by(island) %>% 
  summarise(
    OS_Current = sum(ifelse(bucket == "01. Current", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_Current = sum(ifelse(bucket == "01. Current", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_1_30 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "02. 1-30 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_1_30 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "02. 1-30 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_31_60 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "03. 31-60 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_31_60 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "03. 31-60 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_61_90 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "04. 61-90 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_61_90 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "04. 61-90 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_90_plus = sum(ifelse(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_90_plus = sum(ifelse(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_Total = sum(outstanding_amount),
    NOA_Total = sum(noa),
    NPL= round(((OS_DPD_90_plus/OS_Total)*100),2)) %>% 
  rename(
    Island = island
  ) %>% 
  mutate(across(
    everything(),
    ~ format(.x, 
             big.mark = ".", 
             decimal.mark = ","))
    )

Region

We’re also going to apply the same approach for the region level by creating two datasets: the first will show the outstanding amount, NOA, and NPL for each DPD bucket across all regions, while the second will include a specific cut-off date for more detailed analysis.

# REGION: GENERAL ~> 1 input: Cut Off Date 
region_general <- sqllab_net_clean %>% 
  filter(cut_off_date == "2025-11-01") %>% 
  group_by(region) %>% 
  summarise(
    OS_Current = sum(ifelse(bucket == "01. Current", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_Current = sum(ifelse(bucket == "01. Current", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_1_30 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "02. 1-30 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_1_30 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "02. 1-30 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_31_60 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "03. 31-60 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_31_60 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "03. 31-60 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_61_90 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "04. 61-90 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_61_90 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "04. 61-90 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_90_plus = sum(ifelse(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_90_plus = sum(ifelse(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_Total = sum(outstanding_amount),
    NOA_Total = sum(noa),
    NPL= round(((OS_DPD_90_plus/OS_Total)*100),2)) %>% 
  rename(
    Region = region
  ) %>% 
  mutate(across(
    everything(),
    ~ format(.x, 
             big.mark = ".", 
             decimal.mark = ","))
    )

    OS_DPD_61_90 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "04. 61-90 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_61_90 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "04. 61-90 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_90_plus = sum(ifelse(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_90_plus = sum(ifelse(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_Total = sum(outstanding_amount),
    NOA_Total = sum(noa),
    NPL= round(((OS_DPD_90_plus/OS_Total)*100),2)) %>% 
  rename(
    Region = region
  ) %>% 
  mutate(across(
    everything(),
    ~ format(.x, 
             big.mark = ".", 
             decimal.mark = ","))
    )

We can confirm that the area_general dataset is correct, as it contains 148 rows, which aligns with the 148 areas present in the Net dataset.

Similar to the previous Region: Specific section, this code first filters the data based on the cut-off date and region. However, this time we group the filtered data by area and then summarize it to obtain the outstanding amount, NOA, and NPL for each DPD bucket across all areas.

# Area: SPECIFIC ~> 2 inputs: Cut Off Date & Region
area_table <- sqllab_net_clean %>%
  filter(cut_off_date == "2025-11-01",
         region == "Sumatera Utara") %>% 
  group_by(area) %>% 
  summarise(
    OS_Current = sum(ifelse(bucket == "01. Current", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_Current = sum(ifelse(bucket == "01. Current", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_1_30 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "02. 1-30 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_1_30 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "02. 1-30 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_31_60 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "03. 31-60 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_31_60 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "03. 31-60 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_61_90 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "04. 61-90 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_61_90 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "04. 61-90 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_90_plus = sum(ifelse(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_90_plus = sum(ifelse(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_Total = sum(outstanding_amount),
    NOA_Total = sum(noa),
    NPL= round(((OS_DPD_90_plus/OS_Total)*100),2)) %>% 
  rename(
    Area = area
  ) %>% 
  mutate(across(
    everything(),
    ~ format(.x, 
             big.mark = ".", 
             decimal.mark = ","))
    )

Branch

Lastly, we will perform the same process for the branch level by creating two datasets: the first will display the outstanding amount, NOA, and NPL for each DPD bucket across all branches, while the second will include a specific cut-off date for more detailed analysis.

# Branch: GENERAL ~> 1 input: Cut Off Date
branch_general <- sqllab_net_clean %>% 
  filter(cut_off_date  == "2025-11-01") %>% 
  group_by(branch) %>% 
  summarise(
    OS_Current = sum(ifelse(bucket == "01. Current", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_Current = sum(ifelse(bucket == "01. Current", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_1_30 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "02. 1-30 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_1_30 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "02. 1-30 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_31_60 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "03. 31-60 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_31_60 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "03. 31-60 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_61_90 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "04. 61-90 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_61_90 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "04. 61-90 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_90_plus = sum(ifelse(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_90_plus = sum(ifelse(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_Total = sum(outstanding_amount),
    NOA_Total = sum(noa),
    NPL= round(((OS_DPD_90_plus/OS_Total)*100),2)) %>% 
  rename(
    Branch = branch
  ) %>% 
  mutate(across(
    everything(),
    ~ format(.x, 
             big.mark = ".", 
             decimal.mark = ","))
    )

We can confirm that the branch_general dataset is correct, as it contains 444 rows, which matches the 444 branches found in the Net dataset.

The branch-specific code is slightly more complex, as we first need to filter the data based on three inputs: cut-off date, region, and area. We then group the data by area and branch to obtain the specific branches within the selected area for detailed analysis.

# BRANCH: SPECIFIC ~> 3 inputs: Cut Off Date & Region, and Area
branch_table <- sqllab_net_clean %>%
  filter(cut_off_date == "2025-11-01",
         region == "Sumatera Utara",
         area == "Sumatera Utara Area 2") %>% 
  group_by(area, branch) %>% 
  summarise(
    OS_Current = sum(ifelse(bucket == "01. Current", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_Current = sum(ifelse(bucket == "01. Current", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_1_30 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "02. 1-30 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_1_30 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "02. 1-30 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_31_60 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "03. 31-60 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_31_60 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "03. 31-60 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_61_90 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "04. 61-90 DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_61_90 = sum(ifelse(bucket == "04. 61-90 DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_DPD_90_plus = sum(ifelse(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD", outstanding_amount, 0)),
    NOA_DPD_90_plus = sum(ifelse(bucket == "05. 90+ DPD", noa, 0)),
    OS_Total = sum(outstanding_amount),
    NOA_Total = sum(noa),
    NPL= round(((OS_DPD_90_plus/OS_Total)*100),2)) %>% 
  rename(
    Area = area,
    Branch = branch
  ) %>% 
  mutate(across(
    everything(),
    ~ format(.x, 
             big.mark = ".", 
             decimal.mark = ","))
    )

branch_table
